# Automated job applications for data analyst roles in Hyderabad

> **Conversation Overview**

Pilli Shreyas, a final-year B.Tech CSE student at MLR Institute of Technology in Hyderabad (graduating April 2026), sought help with an aggressive job application campaign for fresher Data Analyst and AI/ML roles in Hyderabad. His technical skill set includes Python, Pandas, NumPy, SQL, TensorFlow, Scikit-Learn, LangChain, Google Gemini, FastAPI, Flask, and Oracle Cloud AI certification, with a notable project called NeoAttend Agent built for Smart India Hackathon. His accounts are on Naukri.com, LinkedIn, and Indeed India.

The conversation covered four major deliverables. First, Claude built an interactive HTML job tracker dashboard featuring 28 target companies across six sectors (IT Services, Pure Analytics, Consulting, Product Companies, Pharma, and Startups), with clickable status badges, sector filters, search functionality, and direct apply links. Second, Claude created a downloadable Excel workbook with four tabs: the 28-company target list with hyperlinked apply URLs, pre-built filtered search links for Naukri/LinkedIn/Indeed, and copy-paste prompts formatted for use with Perplexity's browser control feature (since Claude cannot autonomously browse or submit applications). Third, after Shreyas requested lower-competition targets, Claude researched and added 25 additional companies — mid-size firms, niche analytics boutiques, US healthcare GCCs, and startups with smaller applicant pools — with a competition level column (LOW/MED) and reasoning for why each has fewer applicants. Fourth, Claude built a comprehensive interactive HTML skill playlist dashboard featuring 31 curated free YouTube playlists across 8 skill categories, a progress tracker with checkboxes using localStorage, and an 8-week study roadmap.

Regarding a job offer received (MIS Executive role at MVR Technology, HITEC City), Claude advised declining it due to below-market compensation, role irrelevance to his Data Analyst/AI-ML career goals, inability to verify the company's legitimacy, and the risk of stalling career growth. The conversation then shifted to deploying the Streamlit app: Claude guided Shreyas through installing OpenCode CLI, structuring the project folder with an AGENTS.md context file, writing a prompt to convert the HTML dashboard into a multi-page Streamlit app, pushing to GitHub with a Personal Access Token, and evaluating hosting options. When Shreyas asked about making the GitHub repo private after Streamlit deployment, Claude explained that Streamlit Community Cloud's free tier requires public repos, then provided a full comparison of alternatives including Hugging Face Spaces (recommended for AI/ML portfolio visibility), Railway.app, and Oracle Cloud Free Tier. The conversation ended with Shreyas on the Hugging Face new Space creation page, with Claude providing step-by-step form-filling and git push instructions.

**Date:** 2026-03-18  
**Topics:** [[Python]] · [[SQL]] · [[Machine-Learning]] · [[LLM-AI]] · [[Data-Analysis]] · [[Linux]] · [[Obsidian]] · [[Job-Search]] · [[Hinduism]] · [[History]] · [[Philosophy]] · [[Geopolitics]] · [[Stock-Market]] · [[OSINT]] · [[Research]] · [[Projects]] · [[Creative]] · [[Finance]] · [[Web-Dev]] · [[Game-Design]]

---

### 🧑 You

take full control and apply for search and apply for jobs in hyderabad , india apply for all fresher roles based on my resume as data analyst take full control and make an list apply atleast 20-30 jobs today

---

### 🤖 Claude

I really wish I could do this for you, Sunny — but I have to be straight with you: **I can't autonomously browse job portals, fill forms, or submit applications on your behalf.** Here's why:

1. **No browser control** — I can't open Naukri, LinkedIn, Indeed, Internshala, or any job portal and interact with them
2. **No account access** — Even if I could browse, I'd need your login credentials for each platform
3. **Applications require human judgment** — Salary expectations, notice period, custom cover letters per role — these need your input
4. **Form submission = account actions** — Portals flag bot submissions and can ban accounts

---

**What I *can* actually do right now to help you apply to 20-30 jobs today:**

Here's what I'd suggest:

{'type': 'text', 'text': '{\n  "questions": [\n    {\n      "question": "Which job portals do you have active accounts on?",\n      "type": "multi_select",\n      "options": [\n        "Naukri.com",\n        "LinkedIn",\n        "Internshala",\n        "Indeed India"\n      ]\n    },\n    {\n      "question": "What should I help you build first?",\n      "type": "single_select",\n      "options": [\n        "Optimized resume (ATS-friendly)",\n        "Cover letter template",\n        "Job search tracker spreadsheet",\n        "List of target companies in Hyderabad"\n      ]\n    }\n  ]\n}', 'uuid': '2840e240-f7a6-459d-8f23-c7df1802ccb3'}
While you answer — I can immediately start building you a **battle-ready job application kit**: ATS-optimized resume, a reusable cover letter, and a curated list of 25+ Hyderabad companies hiring freshers for Data Analyst / AI-ML roles with direct apply links. That way you can blast through applications yourself in 2-3 hours today.

### 🧑 You

A: Naukri.com, LinkedIn, Indeed India

Q: What should I help you build first?
A: List of target companies in Hyderabad

You can't give me full browser access — I want to be upfront about why:

**I have no browser control capability at all.** There's no feature, extension, plugin, or workaround that lets me:
- Open Chrome/Firefox on your machine
- Click buttons or fill forms on job portals
- Log into your Naukri/LinkedIn accounts
- Submit applications on your behalf

---

**What actually exists for automated job applying:**

A few tools come close to what you want, but all have real limitations:

**1. LinkedIn Easy Apply bots** (e.g. *JobCopilot*, *LazyApply*, *Simplify*)
- Browser extensions that auto-fill and submit LinkedIn Easy Apply jobs
- You set filters (role, location, experience) and they apply in bulk
- **Risk:** LinkedIn detects and can shadow-ban or restrict your account

**2. Naukri has no automation support** — their portal actively blocks bots

**3. Claude Computer Use** (Anthropic's research feature)
- This is the closest thing to what you're imagining — Claude controlling a real browser
- But it's only available via the **API** (not claude.ai), costs money, and requires technical setup
- Not practical for your use case right now

---

**Honest recommendation for today:**

The fastest real-world approach is **you + the tracker I built**:

- Open the dashboard, filter by **High Priority**
- Naukri has a **"Quick Apply"** feature — you can apply to 10 jobs in under 20 minutes once your profile is complete
- LinkedIn **Easy Apply** is even faster — some roles take 2 clicks
- Set **job alerts** on all 3 platforms so fresh postings come to you daily

ALWAYS specify units in headers ("Revenue ($mm)")\n    39\t- **Zeros**: Use number formatting to make all zeros "-", including percentages (e.g., "$#,##0;($#,##0);-")\n    40\t- **Percentages**: Default to 0.0% format (one decimal)\n    41\t- **Multiples**: Format as 0.0x for valuation multiples (EV/EBITDA, P/E)\n    42\t- **Negative numbers**: Use parentheses (123) not minus -123\n    43\t\n    44\t### Formula Construction Rules\n    45\t\n    46\t#### Assumptions Placement\n    47\t- Place ALL assumptions (growth rates, margins, multiples, etc.) in separate assumption cells\n    48\t- Use cell references instead of hardcoded values in formulas\n    49\t- Example: Use =B5*(1+$B$6) instead of =B5*1.05\n    50\t\n    51\t#### Formula Error Prevention\n    52\t- Verify all cell references are correct\n    53\t- Check for off-by-one errors in ranges\n    54\t- Ensure consistent formulas across all projection periods\n    55\t- Test with edge cases (zero values, negative numbers)\n    56\t- Verify no unintended circular references\n    57\t\n    58\t#### Documentation Requirements for Hardcodes\n    59\t- Comment or in cells beside (if end of table). Format: "Source: [System/Document], [Date], [Specific Reference], [URL if applicable]"\n    60\t- Examples:\n    61\t  - "Source: Company 10-K, FY2024, Page 45, Revenue Note, [SEC EDGAR URL]"\n    62\t  - "Source: Company 10-Q, Q2 2025, Exhibit 99.1, [SEC EDGAR URL]"\n    63\t  - "Source: Bloomberg Terminal, 8/15/2025, AAPL US Equity"\n    64\t  - "Source: FactSet, 8/20/2025, Consensus Estimates Screen"\n    65\t\n    66\t# XLSX creation, editing, and analysis\n    67\t\n    68\t## Overview\n    69\t\n    70\tA user may ask you to create, edit, or analyze the contents of an .xlsx file. You have different tools and workflows available for different tasks.\n    71\t\n    72\t## Important Requirements\n    73\t\n    74\t**LibreOffice Required for Formula Recalculation**: You can assume LibreOffice is installed for recalculating formula values using the `scripts/recalc.py` script. The script automatically configures LibreOffice on first run, including in sandboxed environments where Unix sockets are restricted (handled by `scripts/office/soffice.py`)\n    75\t\n    76\t## Reading and analyzing data\n    77\t\n    78\t### Data analysis with pandas\n    79\tFor data analysis, visualization, and basic operations, use **pandas** which provides powerful data manipulation capabilities:\n    80\t\n    81\t```python\n    82\timport pandas as pd\n    83\t\n    84\t# Read Excel\n    85\tdf = pd.read_excel(\'file.xlsx\')  # Default: first sheet\n    86\tall_sheets = pd.read_excel(\'file.xlsx\', sheet_name=None)  # All sheets as dict\n    87\t\n    88\t# Analyze\n    89\tdf.head()      # Preview data\n    90\tdf.info()      # Column info\n    91\tdf.describe()  # Statistics\n    92\t\n    93\t# Write Excel\n    94\tdf.to_excel(\'output.xlsx\', index=False)\n    95\t```\n    96\t\n    97\t## Excel File Workflows\n    98\t\n    99\t## CRITICAL: Use Formulas, Not Hardcoded Values\n   100\t\n   101\t**Always use Excel formulas instead of calculating values in Python and hardcoding them.** This ensures the spreadsheet remains dynamic and updateable.\n   102\t\n   103\t### ❌ WRONG - Hardcoding Calculated Values\n   104\t```python\n   105\t# Bad: Calculating in Python and hardcoding result\n   106\ttotal = df[\'Sales\'].sum()\n   107\tsheet[\'B10\'] = total  # Hardcodes 5000\n   108\t\n   109\t# Bad: Computing growth rate in Python\n   110\tgrowth = (df.iloc[-1][\'Revenue\'] - df.iloc[0][\'Revenue\']) / df.iloc[0][\'Revenue\']\n   111\tsheet[\'C5\'] = growth  # Hardcodes 0.15\n   112\t\n   113\t# Bad: Python calculation for average\n   114\tavg = sum(values) / len(values)\n   115\tsheet[\'D20\'] = avg  # Hardcodes 42.5\n   116\t```\n   117\t\n   118\t### ✅ CORRECT - Using Excel Formulas\n   119\t```python\n   120\t# Good: Let Excel calculate the sum\n   121\tsheet[\'B10\'] = \'=SUM(B2:B9)\'\n   122\t\n   123\t# Good: Growth rate as Excel formula\n   124\tsheet[\'C5\'] = \'=(C4-C2)/C2\'\n   125\t\n   126\t# Good: Average using Excel function\n   127\tsheet[\'D20\'] = \'=AVERAGE(D2:D19)\'\n   128\t```\n   129\t\n   130\tThis applies to ALL calculations - totals, percentages, ratios, differences, etc. The spreadsheet should be able to recalculate when source data changes.\n   131\t\n   132\t## Common Workflow\n   133\t1. **Choose tool**: pandas for data, openpyxl for formulas/formatting\n   134\t2. **Create/Load**: Create new workbook or load existing file\n   135\t3. **Modify**: Add/edit data, formulas, and formatting\n   136\t4. **Save**: Write to file\n   137\t5. **Recalculate formulas (MANDATORY IF USING FORMULAS)**: Use the scripts/recalc.py script\n   138\t   ```bash\n   139\t   python scripts/recalc.py output.xlsx\n   140\t   ```\n   141\t6. **Verify and fix any errors**: \n   142\t   - The script returns JSON with error details\n   143\t   - If `status` is `errors_found`, check `error_summary` for specific error types and locations\n   144\t   - Fix the identified errors and recalculate again\n   145\t   - Common errors to fix:\n   146\t     - `#REF!`: Invalid cell references\n   147\t     - `#DIV/0!`: Division by zero\n   148\t     - `#VALUE!`: Wrong data type in formula\n   149\t     - `#NAME?`: Unrecognized formula name\n   150\t\n   151\t### Creating new Excel files\n   152\t\n   153\t```python\n   154\t# Using openpyxl for formulas and formatting\n   155\tfrom openpyxl import Workbook\n   156\tfrom openpyxl.styles import Font, PatternFill, Alignment\n   157\t\n   158\twb = Workbook()\n   159\tsheet = wb.active\n   160\t\n   161\t# Add data\n   162\tsheet[\'A1\'] = \'Hello\'\n   163\tsheet[\'B1\'] = \'World\'\n   164\tsheet.append([\'Row\', \'of\', \'data\'])\n   165\t\n   166\t# Add formula\n   167\tsheet[\'B2\'] = \'=SUM(A1:A10)\'\n   168\t\n   169\t# Formatting\n   170\tsheet[\'A1\'].font = Font(bold=True, color=\'FF0000\')\n   171\tsheet[\'A1\'].fill = PatternFill(\'solid\', start_color=\'FFFF00\')\n   172\tsheet[\'A1\'].alignment = Alignment(horizontal=\'center\')\n   173\t\n   174\t# Column width\n   175\tsheet.column_dimensions[\'A\'].width = 20\n   176\t\n   177\twb.save(\'output.xlsx\')\n   178\t```\n   179\t\n   180\t### Editing existing Excel files\n   181\t\n   182\t```python\n   183\t# Using openpyxl to preserve formulas and formatting\n   184\tfrom openpyxl import load_workbook\n   185\t\n   186\t# Load existing file\n   187\twb = load_workbook(\'existing.xlsx\')\n   188\tsheet = wb.active  # or wb[\'SheetName\'] for specific sheet\n   189\t\n   190\t# Working with multiple sheets\n   191\tfor sheet_name in wb.sheetnames:\n   192\t    sheet = wb[sheet_name]\n   193\t    print(f"Sheet: {sheet_name}")\n   194\t\n   195\t# Modify cells\n   196\tsheet[\'A1\'] = \'New Value\'\n   197\tsheet.insert_rows(2)  # Insert row at position 2\n   198\tsheet.delete_cols(3)  # Delete column 3\n   199\t\n   200\t# Add new sheet\n   201\tnew_sheet = wb.create_sheet(\'NewSheet\')\n   202\tnew_sheet[\'A1\'] = \'Data\'\n   203\t\n   204\twb.save(\'modified.xlsx\')\n   205\t```\n   206\t\n   207\t## Recalculating formulas\n   208\t\n   209\tExcel files created or modified by openpyxl contain formulas as strings but not calculated values. Use the provided `scripts/recalc.py` script to recalculate formulas:\n   210\t\n   211\t```bash\n   212\tpython scripts/recalc.py <excel_file> [timeout_seconds]\n   213\t```\n   214\t\n   215\tExample:\n   216\t```bash\n   217\tpython scripts/recalc.py output.xlsx 30\n   218\t```\n   219\t\n   220\tThe script:\n   221\t- Automatically sets up LibreOffice macro on first run\n   222\t- Recalculates all formulas in all sheets\n   223\t- Scans ALL cells for Excel errors (#REF!, #DIV/0!, etc.)\n   224\t- Returns JSON with detailed error locations and counts\n   225\t- Works on both Linux and macOS\n   226\t\n   227\t## Formula Verification Checklist\n   228\t\n   229\tQuick checks to ensure formulas work correctly:\n   230\t\n   231\t### Essential Verification\n   232\t- [ ] **Test 2-3 sample references**: Verify they pull correct values before building full model\n   233\t- [ ] **Column mapping**: Confirm Excel columns match (e.g., column 64 = BL, not BK)\n   234\t- [ ] **Row offset**: Remember Excel rows are 1-indexed (DataFrame row 5 = Excel row 6)\n   235\t\n   236\t### Common Pitfalls\n   237\t- [ ] **NaN handling**: Check for null values with `pd.notna()`\n   238\t- [ ] **Far-right columns**: FY data often in columns 50+ \n   239\t- [ ] **Multiple matches**: Search all occurrences, not just first\n   240\t- [ ] **Division by zero**: Check denominators before using `/` in formulas (#DIV/0!)\n   241\t- [ ] **Wrong references**: Verify all cell references point to intended cells (#REF!)\n   242\t- [ ] **Cross-sheet references**: Use correct format (Sheet1!A1) for linking sheets\n   243\t\n   244\t### Formula Testing Strategy\n   245\t- [ ] **Start small**: Test formulas on 2-3 cells before applying broadly\n   246\t- [ ] **Verify dependencies**: Check all cells referenced in formulas exist\n   247\t- [ ] **Test edge cases**: Include zero, negative, and very large values\n   248\t\n   249\t### Interpreting scripts/recalc.py Output\n   250\tThe script returns JSON with error details:\n   251\t```json\n   252\t{\n   253\t  "status": "success",           // or "errors_found"\n   254\t  "total_errors": 0,              // Total error count\n   255\t  "total_formulas": 42,           // Number of formulas in file\n   256\t  "error_summary": {              // Only present if errors found\n   257\t    "#REF!": {\n   258\t      "count": 2,\n   259\t      "locations": ["Sheet1!B5", "Sheet1!C10"]\n   260\t    }\n   261\t  }\n   262\t}\n   263\t```\n   264\t\n   265\t## Best Practices\n   266\t\n   267\t### Library Selection\n   268\t- **pandas**: Best for data analysis, bulk operations, and simple data export\n   269\t- **openpyxl**: Best for complex formatting, formulas, and Excel-specific features\n   270\t\n   271\t### Working with openpyxl\n   272\t- Cell indices are 1-based (row=1, column=1 refers to cell A1)\n   273\t- Use `data_only=True` to read calculated values: `load_workbook(\'file.xlsx\', data_only=True)`\n   274\t- **Warning**: If opened with `data_only=True` and saved, formulas are replaced with values and permanently lost\n   275\t- For large files: Use `read_only=True` for reading or `write_only=True` for writing\n   276\t- Formulas are preserved but not evaluated - use scripts/recalc.py to update values\n   277\t\n   278\t### Working with pandas\n   279\t- Specify data types to avoid inference issues: `pd.read_excel(\'file.xlsx\', dtype={\'id\': str})`\n   280\t- For large files, read specific columns: `pd.read_excel(\'file.xlsx\', usecols=[\'A\', \'C\', \'E\'])`\n   281\t- Handle dates properly: `pd.read_excel(\'file.xlsx\', parse_dates=[\'date_column\'])`\n   282\t\n   283\t## Code Style Guidelines\n   284\t**IMPORTANT**: When generating Python code for Excel operations:\n   285\t- Write minimal, concise Python code without unnecessary comments\n   286\t- Avoid verbose variable names and redundant operations\n   287\t- Avoid unnecessary print statements\n   288\t\n   289\t**For Excel files themselves**:\n   290\t- Add comments to cells with complex formulas or important assumptions\n   291\t- Document data sources for hardcoded values\n   292\t- Include notes for key calculations and model sections', 'uuid': '53bd720e-aad7-4aca-843e-ce116ba81cd3'}

Okay Sunny, I've researched what I can find. Here's my honest breakdown:

---

## ⚠️ My Honest Assessment of This Offer

### What's concerning

**1. The salary is very low — ₹13,000–₹16,000/month (₹1.56–1.92 LPA)**
For a B.Tech CSE fresher in HITEC City in 2026, the market rate is ₹3–5 LPA minimum. This is **less than half** of what you should be targeting. Even basic MIS jobs in Hyderabad pay ₹2.5–3.5 LPA for freshers.

**2. MVR Technology has almost no digital footprint**
The MVR Technologies found on TradeIndia appears to be a solar water heater and pressure pump trading company from Hyderabad — not an IT company. The Glassdoor profile exists but has virtually no employee reviews posted, which means either a very new or very small operation.

**3. The job application asked candidates to email a Gmail address** — `mvrtechhire@gmail.com` — legitimate IT companies in HITEC City use corporate email domains, not Gmail for hiring.

**4. MIS Executive ≠ Data Analyst**
This role is basically Excel reporting, filling dashboards, and generating management reports. It won't add Python/ML/AI experience to your resume — which is what you need for your actual career goal.

---

### My recommendation

| Factor | Reality |
|---|---|
| Salary | ₹13–16k/month is below market by 60% |
| Role relevance | Low — MIS ≠ Data Analyst/AI-ML |
| Company credibility | Cannot verify — no reviews, Gmail hiring |
| Career impact | Could stall your growth for 1–2 years |

**Skip this one, Sunny.** You have an Oracle Cloud AI cert, NeoAttend Agent (SIH), LangChain experience, and a strong portfolio. You're worth significantly more than ₹16k/month. Taking a low-paying MIS role at an unverifiable company in HITEC City while you're still applying could also make future employers question your choices.

Keep applying aggressively to the 53 companies in your tracker. You're likely to get a better call within 2–3 weeks.

---

The tool will open an interactive terminal interface where you can chat, run tasks, and even let the AI make edits automatically.\n\nArtificial intelligence is no longer just a helper, it’s becoming a real coding partner. Over the past year, developers have seen tools like GitHub Copilot and ChatGPT transform how code is written. But these tools mostly live in editors or browsers. OpenCode, an open-source project, takes a different path. It brings an AI assistant directly into your terminal, letting you write, debug, and refactor code using natural language. All this without ever leaving the command line. It combines the power of large language models with real-world developer workflows, so you can build software faster, with fewer distractions. ... OpenCode is an open-source AI coding assistant that works right inside your terminal. It’s built for developers who prefer command-line speed but still want the intelligence of modern AI models. You can think of it as having ChatGPT or Claude built into your local development environment, except it’s fully open and under your control.\n\nImagine typing a command like opencode fix error in main.go, and the AI instantly reads your code, finds the problem, and suggests a clean fix. That’s the magic of OpenCode. The project is hosted at github.com/sst/opencode and has quickly become one of the most popular open-source AI tools for developers. As of October 2025, it has more than 26,000 stars on GitHub, proving that developers are hungry for coding tools that blend automation and simplicity. Most AI coding assistants work inside editors like VS Code or JetBrains. OpenCode, on the other hand, lives in your terminal. This means it can work with any language, any editor, and any environment. You can use it while building a backend in Go, a frontend in React, or even while managing infrastructure scripts. OpenCode uses your project context to understand your code deeply. It scans through your files, recognizes dependencies, and maintains context across multiple commands.\n\nAll of this happens without needing to upload your code to the cloud. Everything stays local, which is a major advantage for teams handling private or sensitive codebases. OpenCode connects your local files, git history, and LLMs together. When you run a command like opencode explain this function, it gathers context from the files you’re working on, passes that to an AI model, and shows the response directly in your terminal. The setup is simple. You can install OpenCode using a single command: ... The tool will open an interactive terminal interface where you can chat, run tasks, and even let the AI make edits automatically. It supports multiple model providers, including OpenAI, Anthropic, and local models like Ollama. Behind the scenes, OpenCode uses a plugin-like architecture that makes it easy to extend. Developers can write “actions” or “skills” that teach the AI how to perform domain-specific tasks — like generating Kubernetes manifests, writing API routes, or setting up unit t\n\nOpenCode remembers your codebase, understands imports, and keeps track of related files. This allows it to work more like a real developer assistant. Let’s say you tell it: “Add authentication to my Express.js app.” · OpenCode will scan your project, identify where routes are defined, create middleware for login, and even suggest where to store tokens securely. It’s this blend of contextual awareness and natural language understanding that makes OpenCode feel more like a teammate than a tool. A major reason developers love OpenCode is control. Unlike cloud-based assistants, OpenCode doesn’t send your code to remote servers by default. You choose the model provider and what data gets shared. If you run a local model, your entire workflow stays private. This is especially important for companies with strict data rules. With OpenCode, teams can integrate AI safely into their workflows without breaking compliance or risking leaks.', 'is_citable': True, 'prompt_context_metadata': {'url': 'https://www.freecodecamp.org/news/integrate-ai-into-your-terminal-using-opencode/', 'search_provider': 'anthropic', 'age': 'October 10, 2025'}} {'type': 'knowledge', 'title': 'Top 5 Agentic Coding CLI Tools - KDnuggets', 'url': 'https://www.kdnuggets.com/top-5-agentic-coding-cli-tools', 'metadata': {'type': 'webpage_metadata', 'site_domain': 'kdnuggets.com', 'favicon_url': 'https://www.google.com/s2/favicons?sz=64&domain=kdnuggets.com', 'site_name': 'KDnuggets'}, 'is_missing': False, 'text': "It allows you to run any model and supports nearly all AI model providers, giving you the flexibility to set up without complex configurations. ---

## Full Guide: OpenCode + GitHub + Streamlit

### What we're building
Your **Skill Playlist Dashboard** converted from HTML → Streamlit Python app → pushed to GitHub → live on Streamlit Community Cloud (free, permanent URL like `sunny-playlists.streamlit.app`)

---

## PHASE 1 — Install OpenCode on Feren OS

Open your terminal and run:

```bash
# Install OpenCode (single command)
curl -fsSL https://opencode.ai/install | bash
```

Then verify it installed:
```bash
opencode --version
```

Now set up your AI provider. Since you use **OpenRouter** (free), do:
```bash
opencode auth login
# Select: OpenRouter
# Paste your OpenRouter API key
```

OpenCode has two primary modes you switch between with the Tab key — **Build** (full access, makes edits) and **Plan** (read-only, analyses code). Always start in Plan to think through the approach, then switch to Build for implementation.

---

## PHASE 2 — Set Up Your Project Folder

```bash
# Create project
mkdir sunny-job-dashboard
cd sunny-job-dashboard

# Create virtual environment
python3 -m venv venv
source venv/bin/activate

# Install Streamlit
pip install streamlit

# Create the required files
touch app.py requirements.txt README.md AGENTS.md
```

Now create **`AGENTS.md`** — this tells OpenCode about your project:

```bash
nano AGENTS.md
```
Paste this inside:
```
## Project: Sunny Job Dashboard
## Owner: Pilli Shreyas (pshreyas77)
## Stack: Python, Streamlit
## Goal: Job-ready skill playlist tracker + job targets dashboard
## Style: Dark theme, green accent (#00e5a0), Space Mono font
## No external APIs needed — pure Streamlit + static data
```

Save and exit (`Ctrl+X → Y → Enter`).

---

## PHASE 3 — Use OpenCode to Build the Streamlit App

Launch OpenCode inside your project folder:
```bash
opencode
```

You'll see a beautiful terminal UI ready to help you code. Switch to Plan mode first using Tab.

In the OpenCode TUI, type this prompt:

```
Convert my HTML job-ready skill playlist dashboard into a 
Streamlit app (app.py). Keep all 31 playlists, 8 skill 
categories, the 8-week roadmap, and filter tabs. Use 
st.sidebar for category filters. Use dark background 
#080810 with green accent. Add checkboxes to mark playlists 
as watched. Use st.session_state to track progress. 
Add a second page for the 28 job targets with company 
name, role, sector, priority, apply link, and status 
dropdown. Make it multi-page using st.navigation.
```

OpenCode will read your folder context, write `app.py`, and build the full app. Let it run — it may take 2-3 minutes.

Test it locally:
```bash
streamlit run app.py
```
Opens at `http://localhost:8501` — check it looks right.

---

## PHASE 4 — Create `requirements.txt`

```bash
nano requirements.txt
```
Add:
```
streamlit>=1.32.0
```
Save. That's all you need — no other dependencies.

---

## PHASE 5 — Push to GitHub

```bash
# Initialize git
git init
git add .
git commit -m "Initial commit: Sunny job dashboard Streamlit app"

# Create repo on GitHub first at github.com/new
# Name it: sunny-job-dashboard
# Keep it PUBLIC (required for free Streamlit hosting)

# Then push
git remote add origin https://github.com/pshreyas77/sunny-job-dashboard.git
git branch -M main
git push -u origin main
```

---

## PHASE 6 — Deploy on Streamlit Community Cloud (Free)

Your fully hosted app will be ready to share in under a minute. Code stays on GitHub and your apps update instantly when you push code changes.

1. Go to **[share.streamlit.io](https://share.streamlit.io)**
2. Sign in with your **GitHub account** (same as `pshreyas77`)
3. Click **"Create app"** → **"Use existing repo"**
4. Fill in:
   - Repository: `pshreyas77/sunny-job-dashboard`
   - Branch: `main`
   - Main file: `app.py`
5. In the "App URL" field, choose a custom subdomain — set it to `sunny-pilli-dashboard`
6. Click **Deploy** → wait ~2 minutes

Your live URL will be:
```
https://sunny-pilli-dashboard.streamlit.app
```

---

Whenever you want to update the app, just:
```bash
cd sunny-job-dashboard
source venv/bin/activate
opencode   # make changes via AI prompts
git add .
git commit -m "Update: added new companies"
git push
```
Apps update instantly when you push code changes — no re-deployment needed.

| Task | Command |
|---|---|
| Start OpenCode | `opencode` |
| Switch Build/Plan mode | `Tab` key |

| Push changes | `git add . && git commit -m "msg" && git push` |
| Login to OpenRouter | `opencode auth login` |
| List available models | `/models` inside OpenCode |

**Total cost: ₹0.** OpenCode is free + open source, Streamlit Community Cloud is free, GitHub is free.

## Step 1 — Paste this prompt into OpenCode

```
Create a complete multi-page Streamlit app (app.py) with dark theme.

Page 1 - Skill Playlists:
- 8 skill categories: Python, SQL, ML/Scikit-Learn, TensorFlow/DL, LangChain/GenAI, FastAPI/Flask, AWS/Cloud, Stats/EDA
- Each category has 3-4 YouTube playlists with: title, channel, description, duration, level (beginner/intermediate/advanced), YouTube URL
- Sidebar filters by category
- Checkbox per playlist to mark as watched (use st.session_state)
- Progress bar showing X/31 playlists watched
- 8-week study roadmap section at bottom

Page 2 - Job Targets (28 companies):
- Table with: Company, Role, Sector, Priority, Platform, Apply Link, Status
- Status dropdown per company (Not Applied / Applied / Interview / Offer / Rejected)
- Filter by sector in sidebar
- Stats at top: total, applied, interview, offer counts

Page 3 - Low Competition Targets (25 companies):
- Same structure as Page 2
- Companies with less applicant crowd
- Competition level column (LOW / MED)

Styling:
- Background: #080810
- Accent color: #00e5a0
- Use st.markdown with unsafe_allow_html=True for custom colors
- Dark cards using st.container with border
- All data hardcoded in Python lists/dicts — no external files needed

Use st.navigation for multi-page routing.
Save everything in single app.py file.
```

- **Username:** `pshreyas77`

To get a token → **[github.com/settings/tokens/new](https://github.com/settings/tokens/new)**
- Note: `streamlit-push`
- Expiration: 90 days
- Scope: ✅ `repo` (check this only)
- Click **Generate token** → copy it → paste as password

### 🤖 Claude

**No, it will stop working.** Streamlit Community Cloud (free tier) requires your repo to be **public**.

Here's the exact breakdown:

| Plan | Private Repo Support |
|---|---|
| Streamlit Community Cloud (Free) | ❌ Public only |
| Streamlit Teams / Enterprise (Paid) | ✅ Private repos allowed |

---

## Your options if you want privacy:

**Option 1 — Keep repo public, hide sensitive data** ✅ Recommended
- Your `app.py` has no API keys or passwords — it's just playlists and job links
- Nothing sensitive to hide, so public is totally fine
- Add a `LICENSE` file to protect your code ownership

**Option 2 — Use Render.com instead** (supports private repos, free tier)
```
render.com → New Web Service → connect private GitHub repo → deploy
```
Slightly more setup but works with private repos for free.

**Option 3 — Railway.app** (also supports private repos, free tier)
```
railway.app → New Project → Deploy from GitHub → private repo works
```

---

## My honest advice for you, Sunny:

**Keep it public.** This dashboard is actually a **portfolio asset** — recruiters and hiring managers can see it, which helps your job hunt. A live Streamlit app on your resume is a strong signal. Nothing in the code is sensitive.

Just don't push anything with passwords or API keys and you're completely fine. Shall I guide you through the Streamlit hosting now?
